# Task: Document Cilium eBPF Map API

## Objective

Generate comprehensive API reference documentation for Cilium's eBPF map API in the `pkg/bpf` package. The documentation should serve as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.

## Scope

Focus on the Go wrappers in `pkg/bpf` that provide user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. Document:

1. **Core Map Type and Creation**
   - `Map` struct and its primary methods
   - Map creation functions (`NewMap`, `OpenMap`, `OpenOrCreate`)
   - Map lifecycle operations (Open, Create, Close, Recreate)

2. **CRUD Operations**
   - Lookup, Update, Delete operations
   - Batch operations (BatchLookup, DeleteAll)
   - Per-CPU map operations
   - Locked operations (DeleteLocked)

3. **Iteration and Dumping**
   - Dump methods and callbacks
   - BatchIterator type and usage
   - DumpStats for tracking iteration

4. **Pinning and Persistence**
   - Pin/Unpin operations
   - BPF filesystem paths (BPFFSRoot, CiliumPath, MapPath)
   - Map persistence behavior

5. **Key/Value Interfaces**
   - MapKey, MapValue, MapPerCPUValue interfaces
   - EndpointKey as concrete example

6. **Event System**
   - Event types (MapUpdate, MapDelete)
   - DumpAndSubscribe for event streaming
   - Event callbacks and handles

7. **Collection Loading**
   - LoadCollection and LoadAndAssign functions
   - CollectionOptions

## Requirements

Your documentation must include:

1. **API Method Signatures**: Complete signatures with parameter types and return values
2. **Behavioral Semantics**:
   - When maps are pinned vs unpinned
   - Difference between Create() and CreateUnpinned()
   - OpenOrCreate() behavior on existing maps
   - How deletion works within DumpCallback (requires DeleteLocked)
   - Event subscription lifecycle
   - Batch iterator retry behavior on ENOSPC
3. **Usage Examples**: Code snippets showing:
   - Basic map creation and CRUD
   - Iteration with BatchIterator
   - Event subscription and cleanup
   - Pinning and unpinning maps
   - Real-world patterns from Cilium internals
4. **Documentation Structure**: Organize clearly with sections for each category above

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

## Constraints

- Do NOT include file paths or specific implementation locations in the documentation
- Focus on API contracts and behavior, not internal implementation details
- Include enough behavioral detail that users can correctly use the API without reading source code
- Provide accurate examples that would compile and work correctly

     8→// BpfMap defines the base interface every BPF map needs to implement.
     9→//
    10→// Its main purpose is to register a BPF map via value group `bpf-maps`. See [MapOut].
    11→type BpfMap any
    12→
    13→// MapOut ensures that maps are created before the datapath loader
    14→// is invoked.
    15→type MapOut[T any] struct {
    16→	cell.Out
    17→
    18→	Map    T
    19→	BpfMap BpfMap `group:"bpf-maps"`
    20→}
    21→
    22→func NewMapOut[T any](m T) MapOut[T] {
    23→	return MapOut[T]{Map: m, BpfMap: m}
    24→}

    19→
    20→// applyConstants sets the values of BPF C runtime configurables defined using
    21→// the DECLARE_CONFIG macro.
    22→func applyConstants(spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, obj any) error {
    23→	if obj == nil {
    24→		return nil
    25→	}
    26→
    27→	constants, err := config.Map(obj)
    28→	if err != nil {
    29→		return fmt.Errorf("converting struct to map: %w", err)
    30→	}
    31→
    32→	for name, value := range constants {
    33→		constName := config.ConstantPrefix + name
    34→
    35→		v, ok := spec.Variables[constName]
    36→		if !ok {
    37→			return fmt.Errorf("can't set non-existent Variable %s", name)
    38→		}
    39→
    40→		if v.SectionName != config.Section {
    41→			return fmt.Errorf("can only set Cilium config variables in section %s (got %s:%s), ", config.Section, v.SectionName, name)
    42→		}
    43→
    44→		if err := v.Set(value); err != nil {
    45→			return fmt.Errorf("setting Variable %s: %w", name, err)
    46→		}
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	return nil
    50→}
    51→

    53→// is a slice, or the object itself otherwise. Nil values are never yielded.
    54→func iterAny(obj any) iter.Seq[any] {
    55→	return func(yield func(any) bool) {
    56→		if obj == nil {
    57→			return
    58→		}
    59→
    60→		if reflect.TypeOf(obj).Kind() != reflect.Slice {

    27→// checkUnspecifiedPrograms returns an error if any of the programs in the spec

    30→	for _, prog := range spec.Programs {
    31→		if prog.Type == ebpf.UnspecifiedProgram {
    32→			return fmt.Errorf("program %s has unspecified type: annotate with __section_entry or __declare_tail()", prog.Name)
    33→		}
    34→	}
    35→	return nil
    36→}

    38→// isEntrypoint returns true if the program is marked with the __section_entry
    39→// annotation.
    40→func isEntrypoint(prog *ebpf.ProgramSpec) bool {
    41→	return strings.HasSuffix(prog.SectionName, "/entry")
    42→}
    43→
    44→// isTailCall returns true if the program is marked with the __declare_tail()
    45→// annotation.

    47→	return strings.HasSuffix(prog.SectionName, "/tail")
    48→}

     4→package bpf

     6→import (
     7→	"fmt"

    14→// Must be in sync with ENDPOINT_KEY_* in <bpf/lib/eps.h>
    15→const (
    16→	EndpointKeyIPv4 uint8 = 1
    17→	EndpointKeyIPv6 uint8 = 2
    18→)
    19→
    20→// EndpointKey represents the key value of the endpoints BPF map
    21→//
    22→// Must be in sync with struct endpoint_key in <bpf/lib/eps.h>
    23→type EndpointKey struct {
    24→	// represents both IPv6 and IPv4 (in the lowest four bytes)
    25→	IP        types.IPv6 `align:"$union0"`
    26→	Family    uint8      `align:"family"`
    27→	Key       uint8      `align:"key"`
    28→	ClusterID uint16     `align:"cluster_id"`
    29→}
    30→
    31→// NewEndpointKey returns an EndpointKey based on the provided IP address. The
    32→// address family is automatically detected.
    33→func NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {
    34→	result := EndpointKey{}
    35→
    36→	if addr.Is4() {
    37→		result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv4
    38→	} else if addr.Is6() {
    39→		result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv6
    40→	}
    41→	copy(result.IP[:], addr.AsSlice())
    42→	result.Key = 0
    43→	result.ClusterID = clusterID
    44→
    45→	return result
    46→}
    47→
    48→// ToIP converts the EndpointKey into a netip.Addr.
    49→func (k EndpointKey) ToAddr() netip.Addr {
    50→	switch k.Family {
    51→	case EndpointKeyIPv4:
    52→		return netip.AddrFrom4([4]byte(k.IP[:4]))
    53→	case EndpointKeyIPv6:
    54→		return netip.AddrFrom16([16]byte(k.IP[:]))
    55→	}
    56→	return n

    26→// consumePinReplace returns the key names of MapSpecs in spec with the

    44→		name = MapPath(logger, name)
    45→	}
    46→
    47→	return mapRegister[name]
    48→}

     4→package bpf

     6→import (

    12→
    13→// UpdateLink loads a pinned bpf_link at the given pin path and updates its
    14→// program.
    15→//
    16→// Returns [os.ErrNotExist] if the pin is not found.
    17→//
    18→// Updating the link can fail if it is defunct (the hook it points to no longer
    19→// exists).
    20→func UpdateLink(pin string, prog *ebpf.Program) error {
    21→	l, err := link.LoadPinnedLink(pin, &ebpf.LoadPinOptions{})
    22→	if err != nil {
    23→		return fmt.Errorf("opening pinned link %s: %w", pin, err)
    24→	}
    25→	defer l.Close()
    26→
    27→	if err = l.Update(prog); err != nil {
    28→		return fmt.Errorf("updating link %s: %w", pin, err)
    29→	}
    30→	return nil
    31→}
    32→
    33→// DetachLink loads and unpins a bpf_link at the given pin path.
    34→//
    35→// Returns [os.ErrNotExist] if the pin is not found.
    36→func UnpinLink(pin string) error {
    37→	l, err := link.LoadPinnedLink(pin, &ebpf.LoadPinOptions{})
    38→	if err != nil {
    39→		return fmt.Errorf("opening pinned link %s: %w", pin, err)
    40→	}
    41→	defer l.Close()
    42→
    43→	if err := l.Unpin(); err != nil {
    44→		return fmt.Errorf("unpinning link %s: %w", pin, err)
    45→	}
    46→	return nil
    47→}

     2→// Copyright Authors of Cilium

     4→package bpf
     5→
     6→import (
     7→	"fmt"
     8→
     9→	"github.com/cilium/ebpf"
    10→
    11→	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/bpf/analyze"
    12→)
    13→
    14→type reachableSpec struct {
    15→	*ebpf.ProgramSpec
    16→	*analyze.Reachable
    17→}
    18→
    19→type reachables map[string]*reachableSpec
    20→
    21→func computeReachability(spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) (reachables, error) {
    22→	out := make(reachables, len(spec.Programs))
    23→
    24→	for name, prog := range spec.Programs {
    25→		// Load Blocks computed after compilation, or compute new ones.
    26→		bl, err := analyze.MakeBlocks(prog.Instructions)
    27→		if err != nil {
    28→			return nil, fmt.Errorf("computing Blocks for Program %s: %w", prog.Name, err)
    29→		}
    30→
    31→		// Analyze reachability given the VariableSpecs provided at load time.
    32→		r, err := analyze.Reachability(bl, prog.Instructions, spec.Variables)
    33→		if err != nil {
    34→			return nil, fmt.Errorf("reachability analysis for program %s: %w", prog.Name, err)
    35→		}
    36→		out[name] = &reachableSpec{prog, r}
    37→	}
    38→
    39→	return out, nil
    40→}

    36→	// CollectionSpec, even if the code doesn't reference them.

    17→// removeUnusedTailcalls removes tail calls that are not reachable from
    18→// entrypoint programs.
    19→func removeUnusedTailcalls(spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, reach reachables, logger *slog.Logger) error {
    20→	if reach == nil {
    21→		return fmt.Errorf("reachability information is required")
    22→	}

    24→	tails, err := tailCallSlots(reach)
    25→	if err != nil {
    26→		return fmt.Errorf("getting tail call slots: %w", err)
    27→	}

    29→	live, err := livePrograms(reach, tails, logger)
    30→	if err != nil {
    31→		return fmt.Errorf("getting live programs: %w", err)
    32→	}
    33→
    34→	deleteUnused(spec, live, logger)
    35→
    36→	return nil
    37→}
    38→
    39→// tailCallSlots returns a map of tail call slot indices to reachableSpecs.
    40→// Used for stepping into a ProgramSpec when its tail call slot appears in the
    41→// instruction stream of a calling program.
    42→func tailCallSlots(reach reachables) (map[uint32]*reachableSpec, error) {
    43→	// Build a map of tail call slots to reachableSpecs.
    44→	tails := make(map[uint32]*reachableSpec)
    45→	for _, r := range reach {
    46→		if !isTailCall(r.ProgramSpec) {
    47→			continue
    48→		}
    49→
    50→		slot, err := tailCallSlot(r.ProgramSpec)
    51→		if err != nil {
    52→			return nil, err
    53→		}
    54→
    55→		tails[slot] = r
    56→	}
    57→
    58→	ret

    23→}

    27→// take effect in that case. Also note that this does not take effect on
    28→// existing map although could be recreated later when objCheck() runs.

    31→}
    32→
    33→// EnableMapDistributedLRU enables the LRU map no-common-LRU feature which
    34→// splits backend memory pools among CPUs to avoid sharing a common backend
    35→// pool where frequent allocation/frees might content on internal spinlocks.
    36→func EnableMapDistributedLRU() {
    37→	atomic.StoreUint32(&noCommonLRUMapSetting, unix.BPF_F_NO_COMMON_LRU)
    38→}
    39→
    40→// DisableMapDistributedLRU disables the LRU map no-common-LRU feature which
    41→// is the default case.

    43→	atomic.StoreUint32(&noCommonLRUMapSetting, 0)
    44→}

512\u2192\tregisterMap(logger, pinPath, m)\n   513\u2192\n   514\u2192\treturn m, nil\n   515\u2192}\n   516\u2192\n   517\u2192func (m *Map) setPathIfUnset() error {\n   518\u2192\tif m.path == \"\" {\n   519\u2192\t\tif m.name == \"\" {\n   520\u2192\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"either path or name must be set\")\n   521\u2192\t\t}\n   522\u2192\n   523\u2192\t\tm.path = MapPath(m.Logger, m.name)\n   524\u2192\t}\n   525\u2192\n   526\u2192\treturn nil\n   527\u2192}\n   528\u2192\n   529\u2192// Recreate removes any pin at the Map's pin path, recreates and re-pins it.\n   530\u2192func (m *Map) Recreate() error {\n   531\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   532\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   533\u2192\n   534\u2192\tif m.m != nil {\n   535\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map already open: %s\", m.name)\n && !errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist) {\n   543\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"removing pinned map %s: %w\", m.name, err)\n   544\u2192\t}\n   545\u2192\n   546\u2192\tm.Logger.Info(\n   547\u2192\t\t\"Removed map pin, recreating and re-pinning map\",\n   548\u2192\t)\n   549\u2192\n   550\u2192\treturn m.openOrCreate(true)\n   551\u2192}\n   552\u2192\n   553\u2192// IsOpen returns true if the map has been opened.\n   554\u2192func (m *Map) IsOpen() bool {\n   555\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   556\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   557\u2192\treturn m.m != nil\n   558\u2192}\n   559\u2192\n   560\u2192// OpenOrCreate attempts to open the Map, or if it does not yet exist, create\n   561\u2192// the Map. If the existing map's attributes such as map type, key/value size,\n   562\u2192// capacity, etc. do not match the Map's attributes, then the map will be\n   563\u2192// deleted and reopened without any attempt to retain its previous contents.\n   564\u2192// If the map is marked as non-persistent, it will always be recreated.\n   565\u2192//\n   566\u2192// Returns whether the map was deleted and recreated, or an optional error.\n   567\u2192func (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error {\n   568\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   569\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   570\u2192\n   571\u2192\treturn m.openOrCreate(true)\n   572\u2192}\n   573\u2192\n   574\u2192// CreateUnpinned creates the map without pinning it to the file system.\n   575\u2192//\n   576\u2192// TODO(tb): Remove this when all map creation takes MapSpec.\n   577\u2192func (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error {\n   578\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   579\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   580\u2192\n   581\u2192\treturn m.openOrCreate(false)\n   582\u2192}\n   583\u2192\n   584\u2192// Create is similar to OpenOrCreate, but closes the map after creating or\n   585\u2192// opening it.\n   586\u2192func (m *Map) Create() error {\n   587\u2192\tif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n   588\u2192\t\treturn err\n   589\u2192\t}\n   590\u2192\treturn m.Close()\n   591\u2192}\n   592\u2192\n   593\u2192func (m *Map) openOrCreate(pin bool) error {\n   594\u2192\tif m.m != nil {\n   595\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   596\u2192\t}\n   597\u2192\n   598\u2192\tif m.spec == nil {\n   599\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attempted to create map %s without MapSpec\", m.name)\n   600\u2192\t}\n   601\u2192\n   602\u2192\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); All calls to Open() are serialized due to acquiring\n   634\u2192// m.lock\n   635\u2192func (m *Map) Open() error {\n   636\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   637\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   638\u2192\n   639\u2192\treturn m.open()\n   640\u2192}\n   641\u2192\n   642\u2192// open opens the BPF map. It is identical to Open() but should be used when\n   643\u2192// m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\n   644\u2192// writing.\n   645\u2192func (m *Map) open() error {\n   646\u2192\tif m.m != nil {\n   647\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   648\u2192\t}\n   649\u2192\n   650\u2192\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n   651\u2192\t\treturn err\n   652\u2192\t}\n   653\u2192\n   654\u2192\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\n   655\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   656\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading pinned map %s: %w\", m.path, err)\n   657\u2192\t}\n   658\u2192\n   659\u2192\tm.updateMetrics()\n   660\u2192\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n   661\u2192\n   662\u2192\tm.m = em\n   663\u2192\n   664\u2192\treturn nil\n   665\u2192}\n   666\u2192\n   667\u2192func (m *Map) Close() error {\n   668\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   669\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   670\u2192\n   671\u2192\tif m.enableSync {\n   672\u2192\t\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\n   673\u2192\t}\n   674\u2192\n   675\u2192\tif m.m != nil {\n   676\u2192\t\tm.m.Close()\n   677\u2192\t\tm.m = nil\n   678\u2192\t}\n   679\u2192\n   680\u2192\tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n   681\u2192\n   682\u2192\treturn nil\n   683\u2192}\n   684\u2192\n   685\u2192func (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\n   686\u2192\tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\n   687\u2192\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n   688\u2192\t\tduration = spanstat.Start()\n   689\u2192\t}\n   690\u2192\n   691\u2192\terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\n   692\u2192\n   693\u2192\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n   694\u2192\t\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\n   695\u2192\t}\n   696\u2192\n   697\u2192\treturn err\n   698\u2192}\n   699\u2192\n   700\u2192type DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n   701\u2192\n   702\u2192// DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\n   703\u2192// each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n   704\u2192// retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n   705\u2192//\n   706\u2192// To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\n   707\u2192func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n   708\u2192\tif cb == nil {\n   709\u2192\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   710\u2192\t}\n   711\u2192\n   712\u2192\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n   713\u2192\t\treturn err\n   714\u2192\t}\n   715\u2192\n   716\u2192\tm.lock.RLock()\n   717\u2192\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n   718\u2192\n   719\u2192\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n   720\u2192\tmk := m.key.New()\n   721\u2192\tmv := m.value.New()\n   722\u2192\n   723\u2192\ti := m.m.Iterate()\n   724\u2192\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n   725\u2192\t\tcb(mk, mv)\n   726\u2192\n   727\u2192\t\tmk = m.key.New()\n   728\u2192\t\tmv = m.value.New()\n   729\u2192\t}\n   730\u2192\n   731\u2192\treturn i.Err()\n   732\u2192}\n   733\u2192\n   734\u2192// DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n   735\u2192// the slice of all values from all CPUs.\n   736\u2192type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n   737\u2192\n   738\u2192// DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n   739\u2192// DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n   740\u2192// from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n   741\u2192// to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n   742\u2192func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n   743\u2192\tif cb == nil {\n   744\u2192\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   745\u2192\t}\n   746\u2192\n   747\u2192\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n   748\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n   749\u2192\t}\n   750\u2192\n   751\u2192\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n   752\u2192\tif !ok {\n   753\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n   754\u2192\t}\n   755\u2192\n   756\u2192\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n   757\u2192\t\treturn err\n   758\u2192\t}\n   759\u2192\n   760\u2192\tm.lock.RLock()\n   761\u2192\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n   762\u2192\n   763\u2192\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n   764\u2192\tmk := m.key.New()\n   765\u2192\tmv := v.NewSlice()\n   766\u2192\n   767\u2192\ti := m.m.Iterate()\n   768\u2192\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n   769\u2192\t\tcb(mk, mv)\n   770\u2192\n   771\u2192\t\tmk = m.key.New()\n   772\u2192\t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n   773\u2192\t}\n   774\u2192\n   775\u2192\treturn i.Err()\n   776\u2192}\n   777\u2192\n   778\u2192// DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n   779\u2192// if the given map does not exist.\n   780\u2192func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n   781\u2192\tfound, err := m.exist()\n   782\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   783\u2192\t\treturn err\n   784\u2192\t}\n   785\u2192\n   786\u2192\tif found {\n   787\u2192\t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n   788\u2192\t}\n   789\u2192\n   790\u2192\treturn nil\n   791\u2192}\n   792\u2192\n   793\u2192// DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n   794\u2192// additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n   795\u2192// element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n   796\u2192// can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n   797\u2192// In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n   798\u2192// the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n   799\u2192//\n   800\u2192// The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n   801\u2192// object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n   802\u2192// not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n   803\u2192func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n   804\u2192\tif cb == nil {\n   805\u2192\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   806\u2192\t}\n   807\u2192\n   808\u2192\tif stats == nil {\n   809\u2192\t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n   810\u2192\t}\n   811\u2192\n   812\u2192\tvar (\n   813\u2192\t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n   814\u2192\t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n   815\u2192\t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n   816\u2192\t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n   817\u2192\n   818\u2192\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n   819\u2192\t)\n   820\u2192\n   821\u2192\tstats.start()\n   822\u2192\tdefer stats.finish()\n   823\u2192\n   824\u2192\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n   825\u2192\t\treturn err\n   826\u2192\t}\n   827\u2192\n   828\u2192\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n   829\u2192\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n   830\u2192\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n   831\u2192\tm.lock.Lock()\n   832\u2192\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   833\u2192\tif m.m == nil {\n   834\u2192\t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n   835\u2192\t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n   836\u2192\t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n   837\u2192\t}\n   838\u2192\n   839\u2192\t// Get the first map key.\n   840\u2192\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n   841\u2192\t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n   842\u2192\t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n   843\u2192\t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n   844\u2192\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n   845\u2192\t\t\treturn nil\n   846\u2192\t\t}\n   847\u2192\t}\n   848\u2192\n   849\u2192\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n   850\u2192\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n   851\u2192\t// updated while being iterated)\n   852\u2192\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n   853\u2192\n   854\u2192\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n   855\u2192\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n   856\u2192\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n   857\u2192\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n   858\u2192\t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n   859\u2192\t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n   860\u2192\t\t//\n   861\u2192\t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n   862\u2192\t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n   863\u2192\t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n   864\u2192\t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n   865\u2192\t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n   866\u2192\n   867\u2192\t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n   868\u2192\t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n   869\u2192\t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n   870\u2192\t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n   871\u2192\t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n   872\u2192\t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n   873\u2192\t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n   874\u2192\t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n   875\u2192\t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n   876\u2192\t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n   877\u2192\t\t\t} else {\n   878\u2192\t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n   879\u2192\t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n   880\u2192\t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n   881\u2192\t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n   882\u2192\t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n   883\u2192\t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n   884\u2192\t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n   885\u2192\t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n   886\u2192\t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n   887\u2192\t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n   888\u2192\t\t\t}\n   889\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   890\u2192\t\t}\n   891\u2192\n   892\u2192\t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n   893\u2192\n   894\u2192\t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n   895\u2192\t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n   896\u2192\t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n   897\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n   898\u2192\t\t\t}\n   899\u2192\t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n   900\u2192\t\t}\n   901\u2192\n   902\u2192\t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n   903\u2192\t\tprevKey = currentKey\n   904\u2192\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n   905\u2192\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n   906\u2192\t\tprevKeyValid = true\n   907\u2192\t}\n   908\u2192\n   909\u2192\treturn ErrMaxLookup\n   910\u2192}\n   911\u2192\n   912\u2192// BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n   913\u2192// of bpf maps.\n   914\u2192type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n   915\u2192\tm    *Map\n   916\u2192\terr  error\n   917\u2192\tkeys []KT\n   918\u2192\tvals []VT\n   919\u2192\n   920\u2192\tchunkSize      int\n   921\u2192\tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n   922\u2192\n   923\u2192\t// Iteration stats\n   924\u2192\tbatchSize int\n   925\u2192\n   926\u2192\topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n   927\u2192}\n   928\u2192\n   929\u2192// NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n   930\u2192// This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n   931\u2192// when end of map is reached.\n   932\u2192// Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n   933\u2192// the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n   934\u2192// The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n   935\u2192//\n   936\u2192// Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n   937\u2192// iteration over.\n   938\u2192//\n   939\u2192// Example usage:\n   940\u2192//\n   941\u2192//\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n   942\u2192//\t\tebpf.Hash,\n   943\u2192//\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n   944\u2192//\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n   945\u2192//\t\tmapSize,\n   946\u2192//\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n   947\u2192//\t)\n   948\u2192//\n   949\u2192//\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n   950\u2192//\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n   951\u2192//\t\t// ...\n   952\u2192//\t}\n   953\u2192func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n   954\u2192\treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n   955\u2192\t\tm: m,\n   956\u2192\t}\n   957\u2192}\n   958\u2192\n   959\u2192// KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n   960\u2192// of a type T is a MapKey.\n   961\u2192type KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n   962\u2192\tMapKey\n   963\u2192\t*T\n   964\u2192}\n   965\u2192\n   966\u2192// ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n   967\u2192// of a type T is a MapValue.\n   968\u2192type ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n   969\u2192\tMapValue\n   970\u2192\t*T\n   971\u2192}\n   972\u2192\n   973\u2192// Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n   974\u2192// IterateAll(...) is called.\n   975\u2192//\n   976\u2192// If the iterator is reused, the error will be 1037\u2192}\n  1038\u2192\n  1039\u2192func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n  1040\u2192\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n  1041\u2192\tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n  1042\u2192\treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n  1043\u2192}\n  1044\u2192\n  1045\u2192// IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n  1046\u2192// using the batched API.\n  1047\u2192// In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n  1048\u2192// this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n  1049\u2192// of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n  1050\u2192// If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n  1051\u2192// will be returned via Err().\n  1052\u2192//\n  1053\u2192// All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n  1054\u2192//\n  1055\u2192// If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will
